Section 1:
XD4M57Z-1 03/11/2026 JL (H) HSE
House Ways and Means Education Reported Substitute
for HB238
1
2
4 TO BE ENTITLED
5 AN ACT
6
7 To make appropriations for the support, maintenance and
8 development of public education in Alabama, for debt service,
9 and for capital outlay for the fiscal year ending September
10 30, 2027.
11 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF ALABAMA:
12 Section 1. There is hereby appropriated for the support
13 of public education in Alabama for the fiscal year ending
14 September 30, 2027, for debt service, and for capital outlay
15 to be paid out of funds specified in subsection (a) of Section
16 2 of this act and the amounts specified in subsections (a),
17 (b), (c), (d), and (e) of Section 3 of this act. For the
18 purpose specified in subsection (b) of Section 2 of this act,
19 amounts are shown by programmatic area and the total for all
20 programs is shown so as to include estimated sources of funds
21 other than those listed in subsection (a) of Section 2 of this
22 act. For the purpose of this act, "ETF" shall mean the
23 Education Trust Fund and "Federal and Local Funds" shall mean
24 all gifts, grants, contributions, or entitlements, including
25 grants by the Congress of the United States, municipalities or
26 counties.
27 Section 2. (a) The appropriations provided for in this
Page 1
XD4M57Z-1 03/11/2026 JL (H) HSE
House Ways and Means Education Reported Substitute
for HB238
28 act shall be paid from funds in the State Treasury to the
29 credit of the Education Trust Fund, Alabama Peace Officers'
30 Standards and Training Fund, Alabama Head and Spinal Cord
31 Injury Trust Fund, Driver Education and Training Fund, Special
32 Education Catastrophic Fund, Public School Fund and other
33 listed funds and are hereby made for the support of public
34 education in Alabama for the fiscal year ending September 30,
35 2027, and the appropriations herein made shall be subject to
36 the provisions, terms, conditions and limitations of the
37 Budget and Financial Control Act (Code of Alabama 1975,
38 Sections 41-4-80 et seq.), the provisions of the Budget
39 Management Act of 1976 (Code of Alabama 1975, Sections 41-19-1
40 et seq.), and shall be in the amounts hereinafter specified.
41 (b) Amounts shown hereinunder the columns "Other Funds"
42 and "Total" are as set forth for the purpose of establishing
43 amounts estimated to be available by programmatic area from
44 sources other than those listed in subsection (a) of this
45 Section 2, in order, upon consideration of such other funds so
46 estimated to be available, to promote the accountability for
47 an efficient use of funds available, and the same are hereby
48 appropriated by the Legislature. Provided, however, that
49 regardless of the ending date of any pay period which has been
50 or may be established by the Legislature for the payment of
51 salaries of state employees, the entire payment due shall be
52 made from the fiscal year's appropriation in which the pay
53 date falls.
54 (c) All appropriations made in Section 3 shall be at

169 The funds appropriated for Workforce Development are to be expended for those costs
170 incurred by the State in honoring commitments to pay workforce development costs,
171 including services and other assistance and expenses of recruitment and training of
172 a company's workforce, that are undertaken to induce companies to locate and expand
173 their operations in Alabama (described hereinafter as a "Project") and to develop
174 and implement training, placement and recruitment programs that will improve
175 development and expand the State's workforce. Such costs include, but are not
176 limited to: (i) AIDT operating costs directly related to a Project; (ii) wages and
177 benefits for trainers engaged by AIDT for the purpose of a Project; (iii) costs
178 which the State has agreed to pay under the terms of a Project Agreement with a
179 company that are necessary and reasonable charges incurred by the company or its
180 affiliates for personnel providing training to the company's employees, whether
181 those trainers are employees of the company or its vendors or suppliers, including
182 wages, benefits and travel (domestic and, when necessary, international); (iv) any
183 necessary materials, equipment, manuals, or other relevant training materials; (v)
184 the costs incurred for purchasing or repairing or replacing training tools and
185 equipment; (vi) costs incurred for the purchase or construction and maintenance of
186 training facilities; (vii) travel expenses for prospective and current employees and
187 trainees, including travel, food, lodging, relocation, and other costs necessary and
188 reasonable to enable the company to secure a qualified workforce; and (viii) outside
189 training fees. The above funds appropriated for Workforce Development shall be
190 expended primarily for the training of Alabama residents. It is further the intent
191 that contracts with vendors to provide workforce training shall be inclusive and
192 reflect the racial and gender diversity of the State. The Secretary of the
193 Department of Commerce shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of the Senate
194 Committee on Finance and Taxation-Education, the House Ways and Means-Education
195 Committee, the Finance Director, and the Legislative Fiscal Officer any funds
196 allocated for workforce training. Such report shall include a summary of the persons
197 trained and the vendors providing the training. The report shall contain information
198 including the residence, race and gender of the persons trained and of the principal
199 or majority owner of the firm or business contracted with to provide the training
200 services.

354 Scholarship Program
355 The Board of Trustees of the Alabama Community College System, in consultation
356 with the Alabama Industrial Development and Training Institute, shall
357 establish qualifications for the award of scholarships to high school students
358 and adults enrolled in a state educational program relating to the automotive
359 manufacturing industry and shall further provide for the implementation and
360 administration of the scholarships. Scholarship recipients shall be selected
361 by the Board, in consultation with a scholarship committee, comprised of
362 members of the Board of Directors of the Alabama Automotive Manufacturers
363 Association, from applications submitted to the association. The Board shall
364 file a report with the Chairs of the Senate Committee on Finance and
365 Taxation-Education, the House Ways and Means-Education Committee, the
366 Legislative Fiscal Officer, and the Finance Director on September 30, 2027
367 regarding the total number of scholarships awarded for the Fall term of the
368 2026-2027 academic year and the institution attended by the scholarship
369 recipients. The report shall also include the name of each scholarship
370 recipient and the number of years the recipient has received a scholarship.

509 Total Early Childhood Education, 226,595,637 27,208,857 253,804,494
510 Department of
511 It is the intent of the Legislature that the above appropriation for the Strong
512 Start/Strong Finish initiative be used to expand the Pre-K-3rd approach to learning
513 and will incorporate the most successful parts of Pre-K-3rd initiatives in order to
514 establish a strong foundation of early learning experiences that promotes student
515 achievement and success. It is the intent of the Legislature that the Department
516 notify the members of each local legislative delegation (whenever possible) prior to
517 grants being awarded in each legislative district. The Department shall notify the

1045 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related
1046 benefit costs for Certified Academic Language Therapists (CALT) and other
1047 costs of the program. Supplement amounts will be determined by the
1048 availability of funds based on the number of CALT Teachers. The state of
1049 Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any CALT that is
1050 employed full-time in a public K-12 school system or public independent
1051 school and is properly certified by the state of Alabama. The existing
1052 eligibility criteria will apply: (a) CALTs employed on less than a full-time
1053 contract on October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary
1054 supplement. (b) CALTs employed full-time after October 1 will receive a
1055 pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (c) Any CALT employed full-time in
1056 Alabama and properly certified by the state of Alabama will receive the
1057 annual salary stipend. (d) CALTs employed as a substitute are not eligible
1058 for the salary supplement. (e) CALTs who are on leave of absence for more
1059 than half a school year will receive a prorated amount based on the number
1060 of months worked during the school year. (f) CALTs will receive the salary
1061 supplement each year of the valid period of the CALT credentials unless the
1062 Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual appropriation. (g) CALTs
1063 must maintain their CALT credentials in order to continue receiving the
1064 salary supplement. (h) CALTs employed in the final year of their CALT
1065 credentials valid period will receive a prorated amount based on the number
1066 of months worked covered in that valid period. (i) CALTs who leave after
1067 October 1 will be eligible for a prorated amount based on the months served.
1068 (j) CALTs must remain employed with a public K-12 Local Board of Education
1069 school system or public independent school to continue receiving the salary
1070 supplement.

1075 Of the above appropriation, $17,200,000 shall be expended for the Alabama
1076 Summer and Afterschool Program (ASAP) grants program with the objective of
1077 reducing the achievement gap in students who are not proficient in reading
1078 and/or math.
1079 The State Superintendent of Education shall administer the grants process.
1080 Grants shall be awarded to a) local education agencies, municipalities, and
1081 not-for-profit organizations for summer and afterschool programs that
1082 provide direct services and b) to entities that provide support to summer
1083 and after-school programs. Afterschool programs shall be guided by the
1084 Alabama Afterschool Quality Standards; summer programs shall be guided by
1085 the "Final Report and Recommendations" of the Alabama Campaign for
1086 Grade-Level Reading, Pages 81-92.
1087 Data on student and program outcomes shall be collected and used to inform a
1088 continuous improvement process. A report shall be provided to the
1089 Legislature listing grantees and summarizing outcomes.
1090 The intent of the Legislature is to increase access to evidence-based,
1091 high-quality summer and afterschool programming, to build a diverse delivery
1092 model of providers, and to foster collaboration between local education
1093 agencies and community-based organizations. The goal is to award at least
1094 60% of the funding to nonprofit, community based organizations or
1095 partnerships between community-based organizations and local education
1096 agencies.

1209 a. Bullying Prevention Project 5,000,000
1210 To be expended for the Bullying Prevention Project in accordance with Title
1211 16, Chapter 28B, Code of Alabama 1975. The State Superintendent of Education
1212 shall distribute the above appropriation as grants to local education
1213 agencies. These agencies may be awarded funds only after application to the
1214 State Department of Education. The grant application process may require the
1215 submission of plans by the applicant to meet the requirements set forth in
1216 Chapter 28B of Title 16. In the awarding of grants, preference will be given
1217 to applicants seeking to develop and implement evidence-based practices to
1218 promote a school environment that is free of harassment, intimidation,
1219 violence, and threats of violence. This program may also address tier one
1220 and tier two of the school-based mental health model of all students
1221 receiving prevention education and peers working to support and identify
1222 at-risk students. Additionally, the program may focus to increase school
1223 safety through early identification of at-risk students, minimizing
1224 disciplinary infractions including school suspensions and expulsions. The
1225 program may provide grade level prevention curriculum for all students and,
1226 in that case, the curriculum must be updated annually to remain current and
1227 relevant to current trends that youth face in their lives. Any applicable
1228 prevention curriculum must be comprehensive and satisfy the following state
1229 mandates: Erin's Law, Jamari Terrell Williams Student Bullying Prevention
1230 Act, Jason Flatt Act, Price Hornsby Act, and drugs and alcohol prevention
1231 programs. In addition, any program related to mental health should be
1232 flexible enough to focus on the greatest mental health needs for each
1233 individual school. For accountability purposes, reporting data must include
1234 the number of students engaged in the programs, the number of students
1235 supported, and the number of students referred to adults as at-risk.

1270 This appropriation shall be used for the State Department of Education, in
1271 consultation with the Department of Early Childhood Education, to fund a
1272 program to be known as the Governor's Turnaround Schools. These grants are
1273 for the lowest performing public elementary schools which are identified as
1274 underperforming by the State Superintendent in consideration of the
1275 provisions of the Alabama Accountability Act, the State Report Card System,
1276 and other criteria as determined by the State Superintendent. The intent of
1277 these grants is to identify and target specific deficiencies of each
1278 individual underperforming elementary school and target said deficiencies
1279 with high quality and innovative educational supports. In consultation with
1280 these schools as well as the local education agencies that respectively
1281 oversee these schools, the State Department of Education will develop and
1282 oversee a comprehensive plan for school improvement. It is the intention of
1283 this provision that all areas of the State Department, including Alabama
1284 Reading Initiative, Alabama Math, Science, and Technology Initiative, Office
1285 of Mathematics Improvement, and Office of School Improvement, will work
1286 together to best serve these selected schools. Schools previously named to
1287 this list will be known as Cohort 1. Beginning with the fiscal year 2027
1288 Budget Request, the State Department will recommend a pathway for schools in
1289 Cohort 1 to exit this program, and the Department will recommend new schools
1290 to replace those exiting the program in subsequent years. These schools may
1291 be known as Cohort 2 and so forth. The State Superintendent may also request
1292 additional funds so that additional cohorts can be expanded as Cohort 1
1293 schools leave the program over the next few years. Any expansion of new
1294 Cohorts should be modest with respect to the purpose of this program which
1295 is expected to offer extraordinary supports to a relatively limited number
1296 of schools at a time. The State Department of Education should annually
1297 produce written progress reports on these schools to the Chair of the House
1298 Ways and Means - Education Committee, the Chair of the Senate Finance and
1299 Taxation - Education Committee, the Governor, and the Local School Board,

1512 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related
1513 benefit costs for Nationally Board-Certified Teachers (NBCT) and other costs
1514 of the program. Supplement amounts will be determined by the availability of
1515 funds based on the number of National Board Certified Teachers. (1) The
1516 state of Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any NBCT
1517 that is employed full-time in a public K-12 school and is properly certified
1518 by the state of Alabama. The existing eligibility criteria will apply: (a)
1519 NBCTs employed on a less than full-time contract on October 1 will receive a
1520 pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (b) NBCTs employed full-time after
1521 October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (c) NBCTs
1522 who earn National Board Certification in another state and are teaching
1523 full-time in Alabama on October 1 and are properly certified by the state of
1524 Alabama will receive the annual salary stipend. (d) NBCTs employed as a
1525 substitute are not eligible for the salary supplement. (e) NBCTs who are on
1526 leave of absence for more than half a school year will receive a prorated
1527 amount based on the number of months worked during the school year. (f)
1528 NBCTs will receive the salary supplement each year of the valid period of
1529 the certificate unless the Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual
1530 appropriation. (g) NBCTs must renew their certificate by the year of the
1531 certificate's expiration in order to continue receiving the salary
1532 supplement. (h) NBCTs employed in the final year of the certificate valid
1533 period will receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked
1534 covered in that valid period. (i) NBCTs who leave after October 1 will be
1535 eligible for a prorated amount based on the months served. (j) NBCTs must
1536 remain employed with a public K-12 local Board of Education in order to
1537 continue receiving the salary supplement. (2) In addition to the supplement
1538 provided by subsection (1) of this section, classroom teachers shall be
1539 eligible for an additional supplement of $5,000 if in an instructional
1540 assignment in challenging, high poverty schools, subject to the following
1541 conditions and limitations: (a) Teacher holds a valid NBPTS certificate in
Page 63

for HB238

for HB238 Trust Fund Other Funds Total

1914 retain Alabama College graduates by: (1) Identifying internships, co-op
1915 opportunities, and entry-level jobs at emerging companies and established
1916 companies in Alabama; (2) Partnering with Alabama colleges and universities
1917 to promote these career opportunities to Alabama college students throughout
1918 the State; and (3) Creating opportunities for Alabama college students to
1919 learn more about communities throughout Alabama, while also engaging with
1920 other students to create a cohort environment.

2855 Section 4. It is the intent of the Legislature that
2856 any institution accepting funds appropriated in this bill do
2857 so contingent upon their compliance with the provisions of
2858 Article 6, Chapter 1, of Title 41, Code of Alabama 1975.
2859 Section 5. In addition to the appropriations herein
2860 made, all gifts, grants, contributions, insurance proceeds or
2861 entitlements, in excess of the amount carried in this act,
2862 including grants by the Congress of the United States,
2863 municipalities or counties, to any department, division,
2864 board, bureau, commission, agency, institution, office or
2865 officer of the State of Alabama are hereby appropriated and,
2866 in the event the same are recurring, are reappropriated to
2867 such department, division, board, bureau, commission, agency,
2868 institution, office, or officer to be used only for the
2869 purpose or purposes for which the grant or contribution was or
2870 shall be made. Further, all state, county, municipal, and
2871 educational entities are authorized to disburse such sums as
2872 deemed necessary by mutual agreement between said entities and
2873 the State of Alabama, Department of Examiners of Public
2874 Accounts to partially defray the cost of auditing services
2875 performed by said agency. All such sums are hereby
2876 appropriated and reappropriated if necessary to the Department
2877 of Examiners of Public Accounts for audit services, to be

for HB238
2878 expended through the fund established by Section 41-5A-22,
2879 Code of Alabama 1975.
2880 Section 6. The State Superintendent of Education shall
2881 make requisitions to the State Comptroller in favor of the
2882 proper beneficiary in accordance with the law and rules and
2883 regulations governing the expenditure or disbursement of any
2884 and all funds appropriated to the State Department of
2885 Education and/or the State Board of Education in this act,
2886 whereupon the Comptroller shall issue her warrant therefor.
2887 All other appropriations in this act shall be paid after
2888 proper requisitions are made to the State Comptroller in the
2889 manner now provided by law.
2890 Section 7. Nothing in this act shall be construed to
2891 affect or repeal any law authorizing or permitting any
2892 college, school, or other education or eleemosynary
2893 institution of the State to receive, collect or disburse any
2894 fees, tuitions, charges, sales, endowments, trusts or income
2895 therefrom, which are now or may hereafter be authorized to
2896 receive, collect, or disburse. The receiving college, school
2897 or institution shall further maintain separate accounts for
2898 such receipts or shall maintain a system of accounting which
2899 will show a cash flow of such receipts received under the
2900 provision of this appropriation.

2912 Section 9. All encumbered balances of a previous
2913 fiscal year appropriation other than the exclusions authorized
2914 by the Code of Alabama 1975, Section 41-4-93, shall lapse no
2915 later than September 30 of the fiscal year immediately
2916 following the fiscal year for which the appropriation was made
2917 and shall revert to the credit of the Education Trust Fund or
2918 earmarked fund from which the appropriation or appropriations
2919 were made.
2920 Section 10. Upon certification to the Director of
2921 Finance by the State Attorney General that a federal court has
2922 ordered the State of Alabama to pay claims, attorney fees, or
2923 other costs relating to said court order, funds are hereby
2924 appropriated to the affected department, board, bureau, or
2925 commission in the amount necessary to satisfy that court
2926 order. Such appropriations are in addition to any other
2927 appropriation heretofore or hereafter made in this
2928 appropriation act. Such appropriations are conditioned upon
2929 the availability of funds and a determination by the Director
2930 of Finance that other current appropriations are not available
2931 for court-ordered payments.

2932 Section 11. Local boards of education may exercise
2933 flexibility among line item expenditures, not to create a
2934 reduction of earned teacher units and/or local board of
2935 education support personnel.
2936 Section 12. The State Superintendent of Education may
2937 approve a request by a local board of education for
2938 redirecting Other Current Expense funds designated for
2939 pass-through calculations to their local Child Nutrition
2940 Program if the redirected funds do not prevent the Child
2941 Nutrition Program of that local board of education from
2942 maintaining a one-month fund balance.
2943 Section 13. The appropriations made herein to the
2944 departments, boards, offices, commissions, and agencies
2945 include the amounts necessary to pay the State Employees'
2946 Insurance Board (SEIB). The SEIB rate shall be $1,175 per
2947 month for each full-time employee for the fiscal year ending
2948 September 30, 2027. The State Employees' Insurance Board will
2949 adjust the insurance program wherever appropriate to maintain
2950 the aforementioned fixed rate.
2951 Section 14. Notwithstanding any other provisions of
2952 this act or any other act, any amount from appropriations for
2953 the fiscal year ending September 30, 2026 to the various state
2954 agencies and institutions in this act, including
2955 appropriations from the Education Trust Fund, which are
2956 unexpended and reverted on September 30, 2026 are hereby
2957 reappropriated to the respective state agencies, offices, and
2958 institutions for the fiscal year beginning October 1, 2026.

for HB238
1
2
3 A BILL
4 TO BE ENTITLED
5 AN ACT
6
7 To make appropriations for the support, maintenance and
8 development of public education in Alabama, for debt service,
9 and for capital outlay for the fiscal year ending September
10 30, 2027.
11 BE IT ENACTED BY THE LEGISLATURE OF ALABAMA:
12 Section 1. There is hereby appropriated for the support
13 of public education in Alabama for the fiscal year ending
14 September 30, 2027, for debt service, and for capital outlay
15 to be paid out of funds specified in subsection (a) of Section
16 2 of this act and the amounts specified in subsections (a),
17 (b), (c), (d), and (e) of Section 3 of this act. For the
18 purpose specified in subsection (b) of Section 2 of this act,
19 amounts are shown by programmatic area and the total for all
20 programs is shown so as to include estimated sources of funds
21 other than those listed in subsection (a) of Section 2 of this
22 act. For the purpose of this act, "ETF" shall mean the
23 Education Trust Fund and "Federal and Local Funds" shall mean
24 all gifts, grants, contributions, or entitlements, including
25 grants by the Congress of the United States, municipalities or
26 counties.
27 Section 2. (a) The appropriations provided for in this
Page 1

House Ways and Means Education Reported Substitute
for HB238
28 act shall be paid from funds in the State Treasury to the
29 credit of the Education Trust Fund, Alabama Peace Officers'
30 Standards and Training Fund, Alabama Head and Spinal Cord
31 Injury Trust Fund, Driver Education and Training Fund, Special
32 Education Catastrophic Fund, Public School Fund and other
33 listed funds and are hereby made for the support of public
34 education in Alabama for the fiscal year ending September 30,
35 2027, and the appropriations herein made shall be subject to
36 the provisions, terms, conditions and limitations of the
37 Budget and Financial Control Act (Code of Alabama 1975,
38 Sections 41-4-80 et seq.), the provisions of the Budget
39 Management Act of 1976 (Code of Alabama 1975, Sections 41-19-1
40 et seq.), and shall be in the amounts hereinafter specified.
41 (b) Amounts shown hereinunder the columns "Other Funds"
42 and "Total" are as set forth for the purpose of establishing
43 amounts estimated to be available by programmatic area from
44 sources other than those listed in subsection (a) of this
45 Section 2, in order, upon consideration of such other funds so
46 estimated to be available, to promote the accountability for
47 an efficient use of funds available, and the same are hereby
48 appropriated by the Legislature. Provided, however, that
49 regardless of the ending date of any pay period which has been
50 or may be established by the Legislature for the payment of
51 salaries of state employees, the entire payment due shall be
52 made from the fiscal year's appropriation in which the pay
53 date falls.
54 (c) All appropriations made in Section 3 shall be at

55 the program level. Any directed expenditure of funds below a
56 program shall be from funds appropriated for the program.

169 The funds appropriated for Workforce Development are to be expended for those costs
170 incurred by the State in honoring commitments to pay workforce development costs,
171 including services and other assistance and expenses of recruitment and training of
172 a company's workforce, that are undertaken to induce companies to locate and expand
173 their operations in Alabama (described hereinafter as a "Project") and to develop
174 and implement training, placement and recruitment programs that will improve
175 development and expand the State's workforce. Such costs include, but are not
176 limited to: (i) AIDT operating costs directly related to a Project; (ii) wages and
177 benefits for trainers engaged by AIDT for the purpose of a Project; (iii) costs
178 which the State has agreed to pay under the terms of a Project Agreement with a
179 company that are necessary and reasonable charges incurred by the company or its
180 affiliates for personnel providing training to the company's employees, whether
181 those trainers are employees of the company or its vendors or suppliers, including
182 wages, benefits and travel (domestic and, when necessary, international); (iv) any
183 necessary materials, equipment, manuals, or other relevant training materials; (v)
184 the costs incurred for purchasing or repairing or replacing training tools and
185 equipment; (vi) costs incurred for the purchase or construction and maintenance of
186 training facilities; (vii) travel expenses for prospective and current employees and
187 trainees, including travel, food, lodging, relocation, and other costs necessary and
188 reasonable to enable the company to secure a qualified workforce; and (viii) outside
189 training fees. The above funds appropriated for Workforce Development shall be
190 expended primarily for the training of Alabama residents. It is further the intent
191 that contracts with vendors to provide workforce training shall be inclusive and
192 reflect the racial and gender diversity of the State. The Secretary of the
193 Department of Commerce shall report semi-annually to the Chairs of the Senate
194 Committee on Finance and Taxation-Education, the House Ways and Means-Education
195 Committee, the Finance Director, and the Legislative Fiscal Officer any funds
196 allocated for workforce training. Such report shall include a summary of the persons
197 trained and the vendors providing the training. The report shall contain information
198 including the residence, race and gender of the persons trained and of the principal
199 or majority owner of the firm or business contracted with to provide the training
200 services.

357 establish qualifications for the award of scholarships to high school students
358 and adults enrolled in a state educational program relating to the automotive

1045 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related
1046 benefit costs for Certified Academic Language Therapists (CALT) and other
1047 costs of the program. Supplement amounts will be determined by the
1048 availability of funds based on the number of CALT Teachers. The state of
1049 Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any CALT that is
1050 employed full-time in a public K-12 school system or public independent
1051 school and is properly certified by the state of Alabama. The existing
1052 eligibility criteria will apply: (a) CALTs employed on less than a full-time
1053 contract on October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary
1054 supplement. (b) CALTs employed full-time after October 1 will receive a
1055 pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (c) Any CALT employed full-time in
1056 Alabama and properly certified by the state of Alabama will receive the
1057 annual salary stipend. (d) CALTs employed as a substitute are not eligible
1058 for the salary supplement. (e) CALTs who are on leave of absence for more
1059 than half a school year will receive a prorated amount based on the number
1060 of months worked during the school year. (f) CALTs will receive the salary
1061 supplement each year of the valid period of the CALT credentials unless the
1062 Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual appropriation. (g) CALTs
1063 must maintain their CALT credentials in order to continue receiving the
1064 salary supplement. (h) CALTs employed in the final year of their CALT
1065 credentials valid period will receive a prorated amount based on the number
1066 of months worked covered in that valid period. (i) CALTs who leave after
1067 October 1 will be eligible for a prorated amount based on the months served.
1068 (j) CALTs must remain employed with a public K-12 Local Board of Education
1069 school system or public independent school to continue receiving the salary
1070 supplement.

1075 Of the above appropriation, $17,200,000 shall be expended for the Alabama
1076 Summer and Afterschool Program (ASAP) grants program with the objective of
1077 reducing the achievement gap in students who are not proficient in reading
1078 and/or math.
1079 The State Superintendent of Education shall administer the grants process.
1080 Grants shall be awarded to a) local education agencies, municipalities, and
1081 not-for-profit organizations for summer and afterschool programs that
1082 provide direct services and b) to entities that provide support to summer
1083 and after-school programs. Afterschool programs shall be guided by the
1084 Alabama Afterschool Quality Standards; summer programs shall be guided by
1085 the "Final Report and Recommendations" of the Alabama Campaign for
1086 Grade-Level Reading, Pages 81-92.
1087 Data on student and program outcomes shall be collected and used to inform a
1088 continuous improvement process. A report shall be provided to the
1089 Legislature listing grantees and summarizing outcomes.
1090 The intent of the Legislature is to increase access to evidence-based,
1091 high-quality summer and afterschool programming, to build a diverse delivery
1092 model of providers, and to foster collaboration between local education
1093 agencies and community-based organizations. The goal is to award at least
1094 60% of the funding to nonprofit, community based organizations or
1095 partnerships between community-based organizations and local education
1096 agencies.

1209 a. Bullying Prevention Project 5,000,000
1210 To be expended for the Bullying Prevention Project in accordance with Title
1211 16, Chapter 28B, Code of Alabama 1975. The State Superintendent of Education
1212 shall distribute the above appropriation as grants to local education
1213 agencies. These agencies may be awarded funds only after application to the
1214 State Department of Education. The grant application process may require the
1215 submission of plans by the applicant to meet the requirements set forth in
1216 Chapter 28B of Title 16. In the awarding of grants, preference will be given
1217 to applicants seeking to develop and implement evidence-based practices to
1218 promote a school environment that is free of harassment, intimidation,
1219 violence, and threats of violence. This program may also address tier one
1220 and tier two of the school-based mental health model of all students
1221 receiving prevention education and peers working to support and identify
1222 at-risk students. Additionally, the program may focus to increase school
1223 safety through early identification of at-risk students, minimizing
1224 disciplinary infractions including school suspensions and expulsions. The
1225 program may provide grade level prevention curriculum for all students and,
1226 in that case, the curriculum must be updated annually to remain current and
1227 relevant to current trends that youth face in their lives. Any applicable
1228 prevention curriculum must be comprehensive and satisfy the following state
1229 mandates: Erin's Law, Jamari Terrell Williams Student Bullying Prevention
1230 Act, Jason Flatt Act, Price Hornsby Act, and drugs and alcohol prevention
1231 programs. In addition, any program related to mental health should be
1232 flexible enough to focus on the greatest mental health needs for each
1233 individual school. For accountability purposes, reporting data must include
1234 the number of students engaged in the programs, the number of students
1235 supported, and the number of students referred to adults as at-risk.

1270 This appropriation shall be used for the State Department of Education, in
1271 consultation with the Department of Early Childhood Education, to fund a
1272 program to be known as the Governor's Turnaround Schools. These grants are
1273 for the lowest performing public elementary schools which are identified as
1274 underperforming by the State Superintendent in consideration of the
1275 provisions of the Alabama Accountability Act, the State Report Card System,
1276 and other criteria as determined by the State Superintendent. The intent of
1277 these grants is to identify and target specific deficiencies of each
1278 individual underperforming elementary school and target said deficiencies
1279 with high quality and innovative educational supports. In consultation with
1280 these schools as well as the local education agencies that respectively
1281 oversee these schools, the State Department of Education will develop and
1282 oversee a comprehensive plan for school improvement. It is the intention of
1283 this provision that all areas of the State Department, including Alabama
1284 Reading Initiative, Alabama Math, Science, and Technology Initiative, Office
1285 of Mathematics Improvement, and Office of School Improvement, will work
1286 together to best serve these selected schools. Schools previously named to
1287 this list will be known as Cohort 1. Beginning with the fiscal year 2027
1288 Budget Request, the State Department will recommend a pathway for schools in
1289 Cohort 1 to exit this program, and the Department will recommend new schools
1290 to replace those exiting the program in subsequent years. These schools may
1291 be known as Cohort 2 and so forth. The State Superintendent may also request
1292 additional funds so that additional cohorts can be expanded as Cohort 1
1293 schools leave the program over the next few years. Any expansion of new
1294 Cohorts should be modest with respect to the purpose of this program which
1295 is expected to offer extraordinary supports to a relatively limited number
1296 of schools at a time. The State Department of Education should annually
1297 produce written progress reports on these schools to the Chair of the House
1298 Ways and Means - Education Committee, the Chair of the Senate Finance and
1299 Taxation - Education Committee, the Governor, and the Local School Board,

1512 The above appropriation includes funds to pay salary supplements and related
1513 benefit costs for Nationally Board-Certified Teachers (NBCT) and other costs
1514 of the program. Supplement amounts will be determined by the availability of
1515 funds based on the number of National Board Certified Teachers. (1) The
1516 state of Alabama will provide an annual supplement of $5,000 to any NBCT
1517 that is employed full-time in a public K-12 school and is properly certified
1518 by the state of Alabama. The existing eligibility criteria will apply: (a)
1519 NBCTs employed on a less than full-time contract on October 1 will receive a
1520 pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (b) NBCTs employed full-time after
1521 October 1 will receive a pro-rata share of the salary supplement. (c) NBCTs
1522 who earn National Board Certification in another state and are teaching
1523 full-time in Alabama on October 1 and are properly certified by the state of
1524 Alabama will receive the annual salary stipend. (d) NBCTs employed as a
1525 substitute are not eligible for the salary supplement. (e) NBCTs who are on
1526 leave of absence for more than half a school year will receive a prorated
1527 amount based on the number of months worked during the school year. (f)
1528 NBCTs will receive the salary supplement each year of the valid period of
1529 the certificate unless the Alabama Legislature declines to make the annual
1530 appropriation. (g) NBCTs must renew their certificate by the year of the
1531 certificate's expiration in order to continue receiving the salary
1532 supplement. (h) NBCTs employed in the final year of the certificate valid
1533 period will receive a prorated amount based on the number of months worked
1534 covered in that valid period. (i) NBCTs who leave after October 1 will be
1535 eligible for a prorated amount based on the months served. (j) NBCTs must
1536 remain employed with a public K-12 local Board of Education in order to
1537 continue receiving the salary supplement. (2) In addition to the supplement
1538 provided by subsection (1) of this section, classroom teachers shall be
1539 eligible for an additional supplement of $5,000 if in an instructional
1540 assignment in challenging, high poverty schools, subject to the following
1541 conditions and limitations: (a) Teacher holds a valid NBPTS certificate in

1965 Studies Committee (AGSC)/

1968 (STARS)
1969 To be expended in accordance with Section 16-5-8(e), Code of Alabama 1975.
1970 The purpose of AGSC/STARS is to provide Alabama college students with a
1971 simplified, seamless, and streamlined transfer process by providing them
1972 with accurate transfer information through state-approved transfer guides.
